Saturday, 12:47 p.m. - The Very Model of a Modern Magic Metagame
----------------------------------------------------------------


*by **Magic** Maj. Gen. Blake Rasmussen* 
Despite Jund's recent reputation as a format warping monster, Modern has actually been surprisingly diverse as of late. Yes, [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) and friends won both Grand Prix Chicagoand Grand Prix Lyon, but the Top 8 and Top 16 decks were incredibly diverse. Both Top 8s had seven distinct archetypes represented with the Top 16 containing a few other goodies for you deck junkies out there.


So let's take a magical trip down Modern metagame lane and rehash just what you might expect to see throughout the hall and in the feature match arena at Grand Prix Toronto this weekend.


### Jund


Might as well get it out of the way. Jund has been on a tear this year, finishing first or second in just about every major Modern tournament, starting with the Player's Championship, where Yuuya Watanabe took down the title with the help of [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and Co. From there, Jund (and, actually, Watanabe too) took second at Pro Tour *Return to Ravnica*, and a pair of firsts and a second between Chicago and Lyon.


The deck utilizes some of the most efficient spells the game has to offer across a multitude of fronts. [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) and [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) offer hand disruption; [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) , [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) , [Maelstrom Pulse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maelstrom+Pulse) and more offer ways to kill things; [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) are two of the best two-mana creatures ever; and [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) is possibly the best one-drop in Modern.


Plus, ya know, [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) .


Hard to hate out and incredibly adaptable, the deck tries to do the best thing at every point in the curve, and does so efficiently. Recent additions like [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) and [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) have further boosted the deck's power and adaptability. Not only will Jund be heavily played this weekend, but it's an odds-on favorite to put at least one copy in the Top 8.

### UW Angel


Modern Blue-White decks were given a new lease on life with the release of [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) in *Avacyn Restored*. Suddenly, [Vendilion Clique](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vendilion+Clique) , [Wall of Omens](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Omens) , [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) , [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) and [Blade Splicer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blade+Splicer) became even bettera difficult thing to do when you're already talking about cards that ranged from playable to some of the best in the format.


UW Angel is good in part because it's the best counterspell deck in the formatfeaturing [Mana Leak](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mana+Leak) [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare) , [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) , [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) and othersand also because it's likely the best [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) deck in the format. With more cheap instants than you can shake a [Delver of Secrets](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Delver+of+Secrets) at (though not enough to actually include the formerly ubiquitous one-drop), UW often plays like a midrange deck that is capable of switching between aggression and control at the drop of a hat.


It's also unique in that it's one of the few decks that takes advantage of [Tectonic Edge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tectonic+Edge) and, alongside Jund, one of the few to use the *Worldwake* creature lands ( [Celestial Colonnade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Celestial+Colonnade) , [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) and friends).

### U/R Combo


I'm going to lump these two decks together, even though they are very, very different decks. Let's start with [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) , as seen being piloted last by Michael Simon in the Top 8 of Grand Prix Chicago.

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Arid+Mesa)


















The deck looks to cantrip its way into it's incredibly redundant combo pieces, all while disrupting the opponent's plan with cheap countermagic and [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) s just long enough to resolve either [Pestermite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pestermite) or [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) alongside [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) or [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) . From there, every copy of the small blue Flash creatures lets you untap either the Twinned creature or [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker), letting you make another copy and repeating ad infinitum. At that point it doesn't matter how many blockers they have or how much life they've gained, there's not much they can do about a million 2/1s or 1/4s coming their direction.


About the only things that make this deck in any way similar to the UR Storm deck that Olivier Ruel took to the Top 8 of GP Lyonand the likes of Jon Finkel piloted recently as wellare the colors and cantrips. Beyond that, the decks bear little resemblance. Take a look:

[Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMisty%5D+%5BRainforest%5D)

[Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BPast%5D+%5Bin%5D+%5BFlames%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Shivan+Reef)


















UR Storm is an engine deck that looks to chain a bunch of spells together until it can cast a large [Grapeshot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grapeshot) or [Empty the Warrens](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Empty+the+Warrens) . It uses [Goblin Electromancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Electromancer) to make its spells cheaper while [Pyromancer Ascension](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyromancer+Ascension) an [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) let you get double (or quadruple) use out of all of your rituals (mana-producing spells) and cantrips (card drawing spells). [Manamorphose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Manamorphose) , which both makes mana and draws a card, is incredibly important to this deck, and it's likely it wouldn't even be a deck if the odd-looking mana fixer didn't exist.


Why play one combo deck over the other? They both have their weaknesses. Both are vulnerable to hand disruption, but [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) is a little better at winning with the top of its deck thanks to its redundancy and need for only two cards to go off.


Twin is also not vulnerable to graveyard hate, while Storm often is thanks to [Pyromancer Ascension](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyromancer+Ascension) and [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) both relying on that particular zone. Most Storm mages come prepared with that in mind, but it's something the Twin players don't even need to worry about, especially with [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) looming large over the field.


Finally, and the biggest mark in Storm's favor, is that creature removalsuch as [Path to Exile](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Path+to+Exile) and [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) are largely dead against Storm, even though they do hit [Goblin Electromancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Electromancer) . Often players will be caught staring at a hand full of removal while their opponent plays [Manamorphose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Manamorphose) and [Seething Song](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seething+Song) s right to the bank.


### Robots


Whatever you call the deck, the all-artifact menace just never seems to go away. Cheap, brutally fast artifacts backed by [Cranial Plating](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cranial+Plating) on the short list of most powerful cards in Modernmakes Robots the premier beatdown deck in the format right now. Though cards like [Creeping Corrosion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Creeping+Corrosion) , [Stony Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stony+Silence) , and [Ancient Grudge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancient+Grudge) can be devastating, the deck is often fast enough and resilient enough to ignore or even beat those cards.


Of course, that assumes players are even packing such dedicated hate. Without many other artifacts making their presence known in the format, any dedicated artifact hate in the sideboard is pretty much aimed directly at Affinity, and if it's not a large part of the metagame, those can be wasted slots.


But you can never count the artifact aggro deck out, because as soon as players do, as soon as they put away their [Ancient Grudge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancient+Grudge) s, that's when [Arcbound Ravager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arcbound+Ravager) rears its metallic grin again.

### RG Tron


There was a time when there was legitimate argument over the best Tron decka deck utilizing [Urza's Power Plant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Urza%27s+Power+Plant) , Mine and Towerin Modern. Some tried Blue-Red, some had success with Blue White, and a few dabbled in other combinations.


But it was the advent of Red-Green Tron and its uber-consistent collection of the Urza's lands that finally has seemed to settle the debate. Capable of a third turn [Karn Liberated](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Karn+Liberated) with consistency never really seen before in Tron decks, this mana-hungry deck utilizes all kinds of land searching, color fixing and cantriping to assemble its lands in a hurry, culminating in the colorless planeswalker, [Wurmcoil Engine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wurmcoil+Engine) , or something far, far bigger.




![Emrakul, the Aeon's Torn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Emrakul%2C+the+Aeon%27s+Torn)


With [Eye of Ugin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Eye+of+Ugin) , the deck can play for the long game as well, waiting out even control decks as it builds to the ability to repeatedly search up giant Eldrazi. The deck's popularity has waned as of late, but it remains the format's best big-mana deck.







#### David Gleicher RG Tron

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Urza%27s+Power+Plant)


















### Infect


With one foot in combo and one foot in aggro, Infect holds a unique spot in the Modern metagame. One one hand, it attacks with a bunch of small creatures, using pump spells and protection to get them through, and does it all through the attack step.


On the other hand it often kills on turn three.


The deck is pretty simple. Play a one or two mana poison creature, get through with an unencumbered attack, and pump, pump, and pump again till dead. Repeat as necessary.


There are certainly more nuances than that to playing the deck, but the recent adoption of [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) into the poison fold has increased the deck's ability to play a patient "attack for two poison" game. And while it hasn't put up any Top 8 finishes just yet, it consistently places multiple copies in the Top 16.







#### Mario Zuiga Infect


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

### Pod


The last deck we'll go over is a personal favorite of mine that had fallen on hard times until its recent string of Top 8 appearances. [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) deckswhich typically come either Naya Flavored or Four-Colorare really two decks with similar engines.


On one hand, there's Melira Pod, which tries to abuse the combination of [Melira, Sylvok Outcast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Melira%2C+Sylvok+Outcast) with Persist creatures and a sacrifice outlet, often [Viscera Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viscera+Seer) . The result is an arbitrarily large loop that can do anything from deal as much damage as you need to gain as much life as you like, often while setting up your library with what you'd like to draw next.


On the other you have the [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) based ones which, like [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) , try to untap [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) enough to make an arbitrarily large number of tokens to attack with. In Pod, this often happens with [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) , with is fantastic with the decks many other top-notch creatures. [Chord of Calling](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Chord+of+Calling) helps give the deck a toolbox feel, and it's one of the few decks that can play dedicated hate cardssuch as [Ethersworn Canonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ethersworn+Canonist) in its main deck.







#### Ryan Hovis Infect

![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Grove+of+the+Burnwillows)


















And there is so, so much more! We didn't even get to the [Gifts Ungiven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gifts+Ungiven) deck that made the Top 8 in Chicago or the BUG deck that did the same in Lyon. And with such a large format, there are always innovations to be had, such as various attempts at Junk (swapping out the Red for White cards in Jund) and Green-White hate bears popularized by Brian Kibler.


Basically, if you have a plan and can game against these top decks, chances are you've got a shot to compete against the Modern metagame. And if you're looking for something new to break through, follow along all weekend as we look for the latest cutting-edge tech in the format.


 
Saturday, 2:30 p.m. - Izzet's Modern Weapons
--------------------------------------------


*by Mike Rosenberg*

With its massive card pool featuring a multitude of monstrous deck types from *Mirrodin* to today, it's no wonder that Modern makes deck choices so difficult. Earlier in the day, Blake wrote up an overview of the big decks that you can expect to see this weekend. But with each deck having so much going for it, we've decided to dig just a little deeper into what makes some of these decks tick.


For players looking to win with a grand performance, there are a wide variety of combo decks to choose from in Modern. Since there are a few prominent combo decks in the format, we're going to go over a few of the big ones to watch out for. We'll start with a look at the combos of Modern that would make the Izzet guild proud, and later today, we'll check out the more creature-heavy combo decks of the format, Pod and Infect.


Let's start things off with a look at [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) , one that saw Top 8 finishes at the last two Modern Grand Prixs (Lyon and Chicago).

75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Arid+Mesa)


















While there are some unique selections from both Dun and Simon in their respective [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) decklists, both have the same idea: play a [Pestermite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pestermite) or [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) , cast a [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) on one of the two creatures, then make lots of hasty token copies of said creature to attack the opponent for an astronomically high number. Simple, right?




![Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Deceiver+Exarch)![Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Splinter+Twin)

*Why settle for one creature token when you can have five million instead?*

Well, once you factor in that opponents will be trying to keep you from doing this, things can get trickier. [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) s, [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) s, or discard on the right turns and throw a wrench into a [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) player's game plan.


Peter Dun's choice for fighting against disruption comes in the form of his spells. [Spell Pierce](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Pierce) and [Dispel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispel) both let him fend off instant speed removal in response to a [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) targeting his [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) / [Pestermite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pestermite) . This helps against [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) , [Terminate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminate) , and [Path to Exile](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Path+to+Exile) among others, but [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) poses some other problems.


However, the sideboard offers him more ways to fight these cards. [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) acts as a great lightning rod for, conveniently, [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) , but it also serves to protect [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) s and [Pestermite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pestermite) s from well-timed [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) s too. You know what else fights well against hard-to-stop instants like [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) ? [Mizzium Skin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mizzium+Skin) . The *Return to Ravnica* instant can cause even [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) to bounce off of an [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Deceiver%2BExarch).


Michael Simon, who finished in the Top 8 of Grand Prix Chicago just a few weeks ago, opted instead to run [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) and [Mizzium Skin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mizzium+Skin) in the maindeck while moving [Dispel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dispel) to the sideboard.





![Mizzium Skin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mizzium+Skin)



*With [Mizzium Skin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mizzium+Skin) as an option, [Pestermite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pestermite) s and [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) s can shrug off even the most Abrupt of Decays."* 




Both players can also bring in some potent weapons for other matchups after the first game. [Blood Moon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Moon) can spell doom for many decks, as a lot of options in this format are powered by a mana base incorporating the fetch lands from *Zendikar* and the shock lands from the Ravnica Block. And, when [Blood Moon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Moon) is out, they're only going to be tapping for red, stranding most spells that these decks can cast in their hand. [Ancient Grudge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancient+Grudge) serves to buy the deck time against Robots, but it can also shut down sideboard hate such as [Torpor Orb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Torpor+Orb) , which would prevent the combo deck from doing its thing.


With that said, [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) is one of the major Izzet combo decks to watch out for during the weekend. Not only does it have a place in Modern history as the first deck to win a Modern Pro Tour (thanks to Samuele Estratti, who won with [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) at Pro Tour Philadelphia 2011), but it's also hard to argue with a combo that only requires two pieces to go off.


[Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) isn't the only Izzet combo deck lurking around, however. Up next is another Izzet specialty, a concoction that includes instants, sorceries, and one very dangerous little Goblin.







#### Olivier Ruel


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

[Steam Vents](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSteam%5D+%5BVents%5D)

[Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMisty%5D+%5BRainforest%5D)

[Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BPast%5D+%5Bin%5D+%5BFlames%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Shivan+Reef)


















Storm is the other big combo deck to watch out for, and for good reason. It can go from nothing but lands in play to drawing its deck and pointing a very deadly [Grapeshot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grapeshot) at you, and all as early as turn three. And if you don't have an answer for a turn two [Goblin Electromancer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Electromancer) , you could very well be picking up your cards about half-way through their third turn.


The deck involves casting an assortment of instant and sorcery spells that add mana to your mana pool. You then use this mana to cast more spells that do the same. Cards like [Sleight of Hand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sleight+of+Hand) and [Serum Visions](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serum+Visions) help you find these spells, or add to your dreaded "storm count", while [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) lets you sift through your deck while making sure the coast is clear.


But how do you keep playing spells? Eventually, you'll run out of cards to cast. That's where [Pyromancer Ascension](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyromancer+Ascension) and [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) come into play.




![Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Gitaxian+Probe)![Manamorphose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Manamorphose)


![Seething Song](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Seething+Song)

*Okay, so you can draw some cards and make some mana. But you'll run out of gas at some point. Right?*
[Pyromancer Ascension](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyromancer+Ascension) , once it hits two counters, not only lets you double up on your [Pyretic Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyretic+Ritual) s and [Seething Song](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seething+Song) s, but lets you rebuild your hand once your [Serum Visions](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serum+Visions) and [Sleight of Hand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sleight+of+Hand) s start getting you two cards instead of one. [Manamorphose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Manamorphose) goes from a cheap way to alter mana into the best mana producer ever, and [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) become a real deal. Pay 2 life to draw two? Don't mind if I do!


The other card that fuels Storm's engine, and perhaps one of the scariest cards in the deck, is [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) . When you've played all of your [Pyretic Ritual](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyretic+Ritual) s, [Seething Song](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Seething+Song) s, [Manamorphose](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Manamorphose) s, and [Gitaxian Probe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gitaxian+Probe) s, [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) lets you do it all again! Flash back all of those used cards, make a lot more mana, draw more cards, and hopefully you'll find more ways to draw cards or perhaps a way to win the game. Games usually end through [Grapeshot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grapeshot) , which should be for well more than enough storm copies to kill an opponent.




![Pyromancer Ascension](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Pyromancer+Ascension)![Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Past+in+Flames)

*Okay... so you can make even more mana and draw even more cards. But I don't see where this is going to deal 20 points of damage t-*

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/grapeshots.JPG)  
*-oh...I see...*

While Storm can be powerful, it also comes with a few drawbacks. Sometimes the deck just won't get what it needs to keep playing spells. Sometimes your [Sleight of Hand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sleight+of+Hand) s or [Serum Visions](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Serum+Visions) will only draw you lands instead of [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) or more card draw. Or sometimes, even if you have [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) , a well-timed form of graveyard hate, or the ongoing work of [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) alongside discard spells, or simply a well-timed [Spell Snare](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spell+Snare) or [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) , might just spell your demise. After sideboarding, things can get a little bit rougher with cards like [Leyline of Sanctity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+Sanctity) ruining your [Grapeshot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grapeshot) fun. Then there's things like [Ethersworn Canonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ethersworn+Canonist) , which can send a Storm player to Frown-Town quickly.


Oliver Ruel's deck from Grand Prix Lyon comes with some options out of the sideboard to help stifle some of the cards that can wreck a Storm player's day. [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) s let it fend off creatures like [Ethersworn Canonist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ethersworn+Canonist) or [Gaddock Teeg](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gaddock+Teeg) , while [Empty the Warrens](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Empty+the+Warrens) and [Goblin Bushwhacker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bushwhacker) give it a quick way to end games in the event that [Grapeshot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grapeshot) is not an option. [Empty the Warrens](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Empty+the+Warrens) also a nice way to threaten the end of the game if [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) or [Pyromancer Ascension](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyromancer+Ascension) aren't options for continuing your spell casting. Nothing quite says, "So you've got [Leyline of Sanctity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+of+Sanctity) and [Grafdigger's Cage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grafdigger%27s+Cage) ? That's cute," quite like 16 Goblin tokens, especially if you've got a [Goblin Bushwhacker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Goblin+Bushwhacker) for the kicker.


Izzet's got a lot going for it in Modern. With two powerful options to blast it past the competition, both [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) and Storm are decks to watch out for. Later today, we'll take a look at the other other combo decks to keep on your radar: Pod and Infect. Stay tuned!



 
Round 4 Feature Match - Devon Giles (Pod) vs. Brian Kibler (Hate-Bears)
-----------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Mike Rosenberg*
With the fourth round underway, players with three byes are beginning their first round of Modern action for the weekend. Devon Giles, who was piloting the [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker)-powered Pod deck, had quite a first hurdle to overcome: **Magic** Hall of Fame member Brian Kibler.


Kibler, who found success with his Hate-Bears from Grand Prix Chicago, opted to go with it again. Equipped with [Aven Mindcensor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Mindcensor) and legendary goodies like [Linvala, Keeper of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Linvala%2C+Keeper+of+Silence) , would his deck of choice stand up against the explosive power of Pod?


### Game 1


Both players kept, as Giles led off with [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) , while Kibler started with [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) . Giles revealed his Pod game plan with a turn two [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) and another [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) , while Kibler got [Loxodon Smiter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Loxodon+Smiter) onto the table. Giles went to 18 to play [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) before passing back to Kibler, who was quick to drop [Linvala, Keeper of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Linvala%2C+Keeper+of+Silence) into play, as the [Smite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smite) r began to beat down.


With Linvala shutting down any sort of combo shenanigans, along with his entire field, Giles went into his deck with [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) , trading in a [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) for a [Phantasmal Image](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Phantasmal+Image) to dispose of Kibler's legendary angel. A third [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) joined play after that, as Kibler unloaded with [Wilt-Leaf Liege](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wilt-Leaf+Liege) and attack with his bird and his [Loxodon Smiter](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Loxodon+Smiter) . Giles thought for a moment before taking it, going to 7.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r4_kibler.JPG)  
*Brian Kibler's Hate Bears come with a few bonus monsters that can lay some serious beats.*

Giles untapped, then used Pod, trading in [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) for [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) . Deceiver untapped a Hierarch after it made blue mana, and the Hierach then produced white to let Giles cast [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) . This got another use out of [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) , which untapped the Pod, which then traded in [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) for [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) .


Once Giles gestured to his [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) to copy the [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) , Kibler scooped up his cards for the second game.


Giles 1, Kibler 0


Game 2
------


Kibler led with [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) , while Giles followed with [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) . Kibler deployed Qasali Pridemade and [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) ed the 0/1 flier, but Giles rebuilt with [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) into [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) , his draw not short of mana. Kibler went aggressive with [Wilt-Leaf Liege](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wilt-Leaf+Liege) , sending Qasali Pridemade for 6, putting Giles to 11, who was already down life due to his fetch lands and his first-turn [Stomping Ground](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stomping+Ground) .


Kibler's aggressive opener put Giles in a bind, as Kibler sent in for 8 with his Pridemage and [Wilt-Leaf Liege](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wilt-Leaf+Liege) . [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) came down after a [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) blocked, resetting it, as Giles went to 7.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r4_giles.JPG)  
*Devon Giles and his Pod deck can be extremely flexible in its path to victory.*

Giles untapped and cast [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) , going to 9, before passing back to Kibler, who played a land and sent in his team with enough to use [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) if needed. Giles chump blocked with [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) , going to 7 after taking the [Wilt-Leaf Liege](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wilt-Leaf+Liege) . Kibler made some tokens with [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) and passed back. When Giles revealed [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) and the mana to cast it, Kibler offered the handshake.


Giles 2, Kibler 0


 
Saturday, 7:00 p.m. - Phyrexian Fueled Combo
--------------------------------------------


*by Mike Rosenberg*
Combo decks can pack a serious punch in a format like Modern, where some of the game's best search effects, card filtering, and combinations collide to create truly monstrous designs. We previously looked at the Izzet-fueled combos. Now it's time to take a look at the far more Phyrexian of the combo archetypes that people can play.


This next combo deck kills with [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) in a similar fashion to the [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) Deck (which also uses [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) as an additional [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) effect). Pod has been around for a while, and even today it continues to show that it should not be forgotten.







#### Jonas Kstler


#####

##### Mythic (21)



4
[Arid Mesa](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BArid%5D+%5BMesa%5D)


4
[Fire-Lit Thicket](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BFire-Lit%5D+%5BThicket%5D)


4
[Grove of the Burnwillows](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BGrove%5D+%5Bof%5D+%5Bthe%5D+%5BBurnwillows%5D)

1
[Linvala, Keeper of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BLinvala,%5D+%5BKeeper%5D+%5Bof%5D+%5BSilence%5D)


1
[Thrun, the Last Troll](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BThrun,%5D+%5Bthe%5D+%5BLast%5D+%5BTroll%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Arid+Mesa)


















Pod is named after its namesake card, [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) , the powerful little *New Phyrexia* artifact that lets the deck upgrade all of its mana-producing creatures into bigger and better things. When you can start nabbing creatures out of your deck, it becomes a whole lot easier to assemble the one-two punch of [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) and [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) . The token copies of [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) that [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) produces will blink the legendary goblin back into play untapped, which will let it produce more copies of [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) until the Pod player has enough token angels to attack for the win.




![Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Restoration+Angel)![Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker)

The most common kill of choice for Pod players is with these two cards: the angelic powerhouse from *Avacyn Restored*, and the crafty [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) from *Champions of Kamigawa*.



One of the biggest advantages of Pod over the other combo decks is its ability to run an assortment of very powerful creatures that can shut down opposing decks with ease. Playing against Storm? Search out Ethersworn Canoninst and watch the Storm player squirm. Fighting against a deck with countermagic that is preventing you from sealing the deal? Go get [Glen Elendra Archmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glen+Elendra+Archmage) , which can protect the Pod player as they assemble their two card combo against countermagic and removal alike.


Or, if you just want to go off without the worry of your spells being countered, search up [Glen Elendra Archmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glen+Elendra+Archmage) . Use [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) to turn [Glen Elendra Archmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glen+Elendra+Archmage) into [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) , untap the Pod, sacrifice the persisted Archmage once again, and get [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) for a lethally large army of [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) that will follow.




![Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Zealous+Conscripts)![Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Deceiver+Exarch)

[Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) isn't the only way to make [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) go crazy for token copies. Really, once [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) is active, finding the kill should easily come with a little time.



Post-board, the deck also has the ability to search out [Melira, Sylvok Outcast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Melira%2C+Sylvok+Outcast) , which can make an Infect player throw fits. [Kataki, War's Wage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kataki%2C+War%27s+Wage) out of the board gives it some frightening strength against Robots as well.


Pod's versatility to get whatever creature it needs for the job, along with its ability to kill players out of nowhere with an active [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) and the right creature suite to search up, makes this an ongoing threat. However, it is a little slower than decks such as Storm, trading speed for versatility, meaning it can sometimes be disrupted just enough by decks such as Jund to fall short of a victory. Cards like [Grafdigger's Cage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grafdigger%27s+Cage) can also be a nightmare to handle, more so for this deck than others.


That being said, Pod's versatile creature line-up makes hating the deck out a bit difficult. This was seen in round 4's feature match, where Brian Kibler's [Linvala, Keeper of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Linvala%2C+Keeper+of+Silence) was quickly dispatched by Phantasm Image, freeing up Pod player Devon Giles to go off on the very next turn.


The final combo deck we'll be looking with an in-depth breakdown today is the most unusual of the group, but nonetheless feels like a combo. Its game plan involves attacking with a creature, but when you're just looking for an opening to poison an opponent out, it feels like a combo. Infect is one of those decks that can kill out of nowhere, and can have an opponent sweating in those crucial early turns of the game.







#### Jacob Sklar Infect


#####

##### Mythic (12)

[Breeding Pool](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BBreeding%5D+%5BPool%5D)


4
[Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMisty%5D+%5BRainforest%5D)


3
[Overgrown Tomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BOvergrown%5D+%5BTomb%5D)


4
[Verdant Catacombs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BVerdant%5D+%5BCatacombs%5D)


75 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Breeding+Pool)


















Infect has a straight-forward plan. Play a creature with infect, ideally something opponents can't block like [Blighted Agent](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blighted+Agent) . Then play effects like [Groundswell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Groundswell) and [Might of Old Krosa](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Might+of+Old+Krosa) , pumping that creature to 10 power to give an opponent a lethal dose of poison.


But how does it get to that point? And how does the deck fend off creature removal? Infect has a few cards that can let it fight removal like [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) s, and even effects like [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) can get shut down by spells like [Apostle's Blessing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Apostle%27s+Blessing) or [Vines of Vastwood](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vines+of+Vastwood) .


Infect is one of the more aggressive combo decks, as a single creature with infect and untapped mana can represent a lethal swing. In fact, against decks without the way to destroy a creature with one untapped mana, the deck can do its thing as early as turn two with the right draw if it leads with Glistening Elf. Its ability to punish players for waiting to answer its creatures until the Infect player's turn also gives it a fear-inducing effect that other combos can lack. Sometimes, even if you can block a creature like Glistening Elf, it won't be enough in the face of [Rancor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rancor) , which gives this deck another means of punching through a cluttered board.




![Glistener Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Glistener+Elf)![Groundswell](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Groundswell)


![Mutagenic Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Mutagenic+Growth)![Assault Strobe](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Assault+Strobe)

"Turn two kills are rare, but certainly possible with Infect.



In Jacob Sklar's sideboard lurks more ways to counteract an opponent's disruption. [Melira, Sylvok Outcast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Melira%2C+Sylvok+Outcast) or creatures like [Thalia, Guardian of Thraben](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thalia%2C+Guardian+of+Thraben) , both known for mucking up this deck's kills, will have a hard time standing up to a full set of of [Dismember](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dismember) s to let its creatures do its poisonous job.


So, it's clear that Infect can pack a punch. But where are its shortcomings? Sometimes, an Infect player can run out of poisonous creatures to deploy. Other times, it can lack the necessary pump effects to get it there in time. After all, there are other decks in this format are fast, and Infect is burdened by needing a creature to do its dirty work through a scary combat phase.


These two ferocious Phyrexian fueled combos, along with the previous two Izzet inspired combos, are just some of the decks you can find in the Modern format. There's more that makes up the Modern masterpieces that we'll see here this weekend, and we'll just have to see how Modern continues to evolve with each event.


 
Round 5 Feature Match - Ari Lax vs. Matt Nass
---------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
Ari Lax and Matt Nass are two players who have occasionally put up brilliant results while teetering just on the edge of making the jump to full-time pros. Both have been prolific writers online and have, at times, been cited as up and comers in the world of **Magic**.


Today, Nass was piloting the [Channel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Channel) fireball Jund deck with [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) against Lax's metagame choice of 4-Color [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) . Lax had been playing Poison in Modern for some time, but opted to make the switch when [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) became the de facto three drop in Jund. He chose it specifically for its ability to battle the powerful sorcery, something Poison had a difficult time doing.


Lax got another boost when he was able to keep his seven as Nass sent back a hand that that, in his mind, was pretty iffy.


"I keep a lot of borderline hands," Lax said, citing [Tempered Steel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tempered+Steel) of a few season ago for ruining his mulligan decisions.


Now to see if this one was borderline, or if Lax could punish Nass's muted start.


### Game 1


[Breeding Pool](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breeding+Pool) into [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) was exactly how Lax's [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) deck wanted to kick things off, but Nass had his own dangerous one-drop as well, starting with the imposing and ever present [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) .


[Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) allowed Lax to [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) Nass's [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) on upkeep to slow down a potentially fast Jund start, but [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) revealed [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) , [Murderous Redcap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murderous+Redcap) and [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) . Nass didn't even hesitate taking the deck's namesake artifact, even with the possibility of a turn four combo kill [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) could represent.


Lax continued to take damage from his shock lands, dropping to 13 as he played a freshly drawn [Glen Elendra Archmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glen+Elendra+Archmage) . The front half of the Faerie died to [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) immediately before Nass cast [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) , turning up an [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) that missed on targets (Kiki Jiki and [Murderous Redcap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murderous+Redcap) ).



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r5_nass.JPG)  
*Matt Nass found his Jund deck befuddled and silenced at every turn in Game 1.*

Another good draw gave Lax a [Linvala, Keeper of Silence](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Linvala%2C+Keeper+of+Silence) , shutting off [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) for the time being and providing a brick wall for Nass to try and claw his way through.


Lax's next attack with Linvala dropped Nass to just four life, and when Nass couldn't hope to resolve a [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) through the active Glen Elendra Archmange, he conceded the first game.


Ari Lax 1Matt Nass 0


Game 2
------


Between games, the players and friends discussed the differences between Lax's Pod deck and the Melira Pod deck advocated by Sam Black. Nass thought Melira won more games without going to its combo, but at the same time probably made worse use of [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) than Lax's Blue Naya version. Nass thought the mana was worse too, particularly [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) and his three red mana.


"Eh, it's a little awkward to cast," Lax admitted, having just had it in hand with only one red source in the previous game.


But that awkwardness didn't stop Lax from keeping yet another seven while Nass, once again, dropped to six cards without hesitation.


But Nass started making up for that the following turn with a [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) that got to work building his hand back up. Lax had a turn two [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) to try and slow Nass down, but a pair of [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) s was plenty of action for the Jund player.


[Obstinate Baloth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Obstinate+Baloth) jumped Lax to 22 after playing a [Steam Vents](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steam+Vents) untapped, while Nass fell to 13 when [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) flipped off the [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) trigger.


"Bink!" Lax said. "Not really bink, but, don't worry about it."


Lax openly bemoaned not playing his [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) in combat in case [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) attacked, but ultimately Lax decided he had too much respect for Nass to expect he would attack into it.


[Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) revealed two lands, [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) and [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) , eventually stealing the Legendary Goblin, , and Nass followed up with [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) to continue building his forces. Nass was way ahead, but at just 11 life, he could be in trouble.


Nass had agonized over the [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) decision, as Lax only had two red sources available, but already had the [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) for the combo kill should he draw a third. Still, [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) represented a ton of damage. When Lax played a topdecked third red source on the next turn, Nass was certainly relieved.


[Predict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Predict) ably, Lax used [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) to steal [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and attack with it, the Baloth and the Conscripts.


After blocks and a [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) activation, Nass fell to six life, but turned over a land on his upkeep to stay there. [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) flipped up a [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) , which Nass declined to cast since he knew Lax held only a land in hand.


[Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) let Lax re-use his [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) to steal [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) , though he immediately regretted his decision, wishing he had simply given haste to his [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) to keep Nass from blocking it at all.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r5_lax.JPG)  
*Tweaking and tuning his deck to handle a Spirit Jund dominated metagame, Ari Lax's [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) deck was humming along smoothly. "When you have [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) in play, it's the best deck in Modern," he said.* 

Nass fiddled with his blocking options, trying to find the best configuration he could to keep his head, and his life total, above water. He went over the options several times before finally settling on the option that killed [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) and a [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) , but left him at two life.


At this point, Lax had no cards in hand but a 3/4 flier that was immediately lethal if Nass couldn't answer it.


[Terminate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminate) killed the [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) , but Nass still had to deal with the now GavonyTownship-powered force headed his way. He managed to survive the turn, but drew only land in his draw step. When several turns gave him no answers besides chump blocking, Nass conceded in the face of a pair of 3/4 [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) .


"I'm not very good with [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) ," Nass bemoaned, having whiffed on [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) and declined to cast [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) .


Lax 2Nass 0


 
Saturday, 6:00 p.m. - Single Card Spotlight: [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls)
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
Banned in Block. Featured prominently in Legacy. Part-time metagame monster in Standard. And, these days, practically undisputed best three drop in Modern.


[Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) is all of these things and more, a strong resume for a card that, on its surface, doesn't look like much more than double [Midnight Haunting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Midnight+Haunting) .




![Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Lingering+Souls)![Midnight Haunting](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Midnight+Haunting)

In this case, one really is better than two.



But it's much, much more than that.


[Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) is whatever the deck wants it to be. It can be an efficient way to create a fleet of attacking flyers or it can be a cheap way to create a bunch of chump blockers. It can push through card advantage with its Flashbackespecially in conjunction with something like [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) and it can push through damage by spreading out its four power over four creatures.


It also slices, dices, and rubs Jace's shoulders after a long day of reading minds. It does it all.


It even warps deck choices. The adoption of [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) in Modern has had a profound affect on the format. Jund has gone so far as to splash white just for [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) , dropping [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) or [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger) in favor of making a bunch of Spirits. In fact, [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) was itself something of a metagame choice, as Finks and Messenger became much worse when everyone started playing [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) s capable of exiling them for value before they can even Persist back.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/geralfFinks.JPG)  
*These cards used to be good...*

Melissa De Tora has even gone so far as to build her deck around [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) ' main function: making tokens. Sporting a Black-White token deck, [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) serves as the centerpiece of her token-making strategy, supplanting (though not fully replacing) [Spectral Procession](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spectral+Procession) as the best incentive to take that path.


But even decks that aren't playing it have become acutely aware of its presence. Ari Lax, who has long been an advocate of Poison, dropped his Infect creatures in favor of [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) , almost entirely on the back of [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) .


"Jund wasn't a bad matchup for Poison in the first place, but [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) made it really hard to punch through," Lax said. "I tried [Distortion Strike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Distortion+Strike) , but it wasn't consistent enough."


Instead, he chose to play Kiki Pod, a deck capable of creating an arbitrarily large number of attackers, making [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) virtually irrelevant.


Also on the rise this month is [Izzet Staticaster](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Staticaster) . Already making waves in Standard, the flashiest pinger laughs at [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) and has been popping up in Blue-White-Red decks and as a tutor target in [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) lists.


On the other side of the coin, the [Channel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Channel) fireball crew has adopted an "if you can't beat it, join 'em" mentality, once again sleeving up the Spirit Jund decks most of them brought to Chicago last month.


The card is so good a crew led by Reid Duke is playing an aggressive 5-color [Tribal Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribal+Flames) deck that has affectionately been called Haunted Zoo. William "Huey" Jensen [won a grinder with it](http://www.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=mtg/daily/eventcoverage/gptor12/welcome#1), and there seem to be a number of players running the list this weekend.


I mean, how cool is [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) into [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) ? I mean, assuming you're not on the receiving end.




![Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Bloodbraid+Elf)![Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Lingering+Souls)

Modern: Where this is a thing.



Add to all of that the [Gifts Ungiven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gifts+Ungiven) deck that made the Top 8 of Chicago, plus various Junk (Black-Green-White) decks, and the various random decks that populate a Grand Prix, and [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) very well could be one of the most influential cards in Toronto this weekend.


The only question left is, how will you adapt?


 
Round 6 Feature Match - Alexander Hayne (Melira Pod) vs. Ben Stark (Scapeshift)
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Mike Rosenberg*
Pro Tour *Avacyn Restored* champion Alexander Hayne saw plenty of success during the previous season. Today, he gets a chance to play at a Grand Prix that is a little closer to home. His opponent, Ben Stark of Team ChannelFireball, sat down ready to race with his [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) deck. Hayne's Merlia Pod deck had some great lines of play, but with Stark's disruption, who would be able to combo off first?


### Game 1


Hayne won the die roll and elected to go first. Hayne had the first play with a second-turn [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) , while Stark immediately dispensed of it with an [Izzet Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Charm) . Hayne used a [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) , found an untapped [Overgrown Tomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overgrown+Tomb) , and then went to 14 in order to play [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) .



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r6_stark.JPG)  
*Ben Stark's [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) deck does what it can to keep Hayne's Pod deck at bay, while building up lands for his big turn.* 

Stark had no action on the third turn, while Hayne unloaded with another [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) . Stark dug with [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) , finding another [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) , and on the fourth turn a [Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek) accelerated his mana base a little bit more. He passed back with two mana open.


" [Viscera Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viscera+Seer) ," Hayne announced, which Stark let resolve. Pod #1 turned [Viscera Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viscera+Seer) into Merlia, Sylvok Outcast, and Pod #2 turned Melira into [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) . Stark used his [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) at the end of the turn, finding [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) . Stark untapped, played [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) along with a land, and passed back with four open. [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) swung for 3, and a Pod turned [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) (which immediately came back) for [Ranger of Eos](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ranger+of+Eos) , which found [Viscera Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viscera+Seer) and [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) .


Stark allowed [Viscera Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viscera+Seer) to resolve, and Hayne used his second Pod to turn [Ranger of Eos](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ranger+of+Eos) into [Reveillark](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Reveillark) . He passed back to Stark, who used [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to flash back [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) . He picked up his five cards and grimaced, " [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) s are not forthcoming this round," he said, debating over the correct choice.


He eventually went with another [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) . He used it on his next turn, and this time, [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) was forthcoming. He cast the brutal four mana sorcery, and after showing Hayne the necessary lands with [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) , Hayne picked up his cards for the second game.


Hayne 0  Stark 1


"Putting me on Bluffshift?" Stark asked jokingly. "You never know!" Hayne said, saying that he just wanted to confirm that there were enough [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) s to go with [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle) for the first game.


### Game 2


Hayne led off with a tapped land, while Stark got started with [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) into a [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus) . [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) came down for Hayne, as Stark went to 17 off of [Steam Vents](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Steam+Vents) to cast [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) . [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) and [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) gave him some hefty acceleration, as Hayne passed back with [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) mana available for his [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) . Stark played a tapped [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) and passed back with three open. Hayne searched up [Burrenton Forge-Tender](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burrenton+Forge-Tender) , discarding [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) .


Hayne sent [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) in, which became a 3/3 due to [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) . When Stark had no effects, Hayne used his [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) , to which Stark responded with [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) for [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) . The attack put Stark down to 13, who popped his [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus) before untapping.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r6_hayne.JPG)  
*Alexander Hayne's Pod deck puts on the pressure, making each play from Stark a potential danger.*

Stark passed after playing a fifth land, and Hayne cast [Burrenton Forge-Tender](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burrenton+Forge-Tender) . He passed, and when Stark attempted to fetch with [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) , Hayne used [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) mana and [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) to dig up [Aven Mindcensor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Mindcensor) . Hayne attempted to play the creature, but Stark had [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) to keep it locked in Hayne's hand for the time being.


Stark grimaced, and played a second [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) before passing with five mana open. [Fauna Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fauna+Shaman) went in for 4 on the following turn, but when Hayne attempted a [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) , [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) sent it back. [Birds of Paradise](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birds+of+Paradise) joined his team as Hayne passed back with mana open for the [Aven Mindcensor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Mindcensor) .


Stark drew, cast [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) , a [Stomping Ground](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stomping+Ground) , and passed. Hayne attempted [Aven Mindcensor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aven+Mindcensor) , but a third [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) sent it back to Hayne's hand. Hayne, however, stuck the bird on his next turn during the main phase, as Stark was forced to pop his [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) in response. Attacks put Stark to 3, and Hayne passed after playing [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) .


Stark used [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) , which found [Firespout](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firespout) . He played it on his turn, forcing Hayne to use the [Burrenton Forge-Tender](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burrenton+Forge-Tender) , but [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) to recast a new [Firespout](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firespout) , free from the Kithkin's damage prevention, cleared away everything but [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) . Hayne, out of gas, played [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) and passed back.


With the coast clear, Stark cast [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) . He sacrificed six lands and found six [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) s via his shock lands to go with his two [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) s, which was enough to burn through Hayne even with [Spellskite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Spellskite) in play.


Hayne 0, Stark 2


 
Saturday, 7:00 p.m. - Card Feature: [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman)
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Mike Rosenberg*
In the Modern format, players play the best cards from *Mirrodin* to *Return to Ravnica*, and Eight Edition to **Magic** 2013.
