The fastest creatures, the most powerful instants, the most efficient lands, and some of the greatest hits from Standards past and present collide in a rag-tag format that challenges a player's mental awareness, deck-building genius, and critical thinking.


In a format such as this, every zone is prominent part of the game. Acceleration is important in a fast format, and keeping the graveyard at bay is equally important in a format that uses it for all kinds of dastardly deeds. So what more can you ask for when a creature can pull double duty, accelerating you into the speedy starts that your deck requires while also keeping players from being unfair with their graveyard?


[Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) , one of the big break-out hits of *Return to Ravnica* for Modern and Legacy, is capable of doing it all, and as expected, it's being seen at Grand Prix Toronto en masse.




![Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Deathrite+Shaman)

[Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) is the undisputed breakout card of *Return to Ravnica* for the Modern format, offering a little bit of something that everyone could use in this fast format.



With the cycle of fetch lands from *Zendikar* part of the Modern format ( [Verdant Catacombs](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Verdant+Catacombs) , [Misty Rainforest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Misty+Rainforest) , etc), [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) is consistently tapping for any color of mana when it needs to, allowing players to accelerate into some devastating turn two and turn three plays. What do you think of an early [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) ? How about [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) ? Perhaps a turn two [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) is your thing, as [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) gives that deck yet another great mana producer.


The existence of this seemingly simple one-mana creature has almost entirely pushed out [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) and [Geralf's Messenger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geralf%27s+Messenger) from the current Jund lists being seen here this weekend. In fact, most popular Jund players have instead moved to a version that packs [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) , as Blake detailed in his feature on the powerful *Dark Ascension* sorcery.




![Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Lingering+Souls)![Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kitchen+Finks)

[Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) eventually replaced [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) in Jund decks, as it not only did what needed to be done a little bit better, but it was also a little less vulnerable to [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) 's effect.



But [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) can be good against that as well! If an opponent can't cast and immediately flash back [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) , [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) 's ability can exile the brutal sorcery before it can be used for two more spirit tokens on the following turn, making [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) an unhealthy prospect against an active Deathrite.


[Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) 's place in Pod has also been established, as Alexander Hayne has shown off so far this weekend. In his round 6 feature match, [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) put in some serious work against Hayne's Jund opponent, with four exiled sorcery cards bringing the Jund player down low enough to die to an all-in attack aided by [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) .


[Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) even gives players another way to fight combo decks such as Storm, as exiling one instant or sorcery after another renders powerful combo-keys like [Past in Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Past+in+Flames) and [Pyromancer Ascension](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pyromancer+Ascension) powerless.


As Modern continues to change, there's one thing we're lefting wondering: will decks adept to [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) 's existence, or will more people continue to adapt him in their own decks? Only time will tell, but one thing's certain. We're certainly not done seeing this card in the feature match area this weekend.


 
Round 7 Feature Match - Brian Liu vs. Pat Cox
---------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
While a lot of players came into the weekend expecting to attend GP Jund, the sheer variety of decks present on Day 1 has given a completely different, dynamic picture of the format. And our feature matches this round were no different.


On one side, we had Pat Cox, who chose [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) specifically because he didn't want to play Jund mirrors. On the other, Brian Liu, who brought a "combo" deck of his own with Kiki Pod, looking to pressure Cox with a menagerie of creatures, all of which immediately improve when [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) is in play.


### Game 1


Winning his first die roll of the weekend, Pat Cox took the play as both players kept their initial seven and led with a [Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek) on turn two and Sakura Tribe Elder plus [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) (finding [Firespout](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Firespout) ) on turn three. [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap) caster on [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) on turn four simply found another [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) , which in turn found yet ANOTHER [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) .


Liu, meanwhile, had nothing but lands for his first two turns before resolving [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) . His follow up [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) was hit with [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) , but he was able to resolve [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) before passing the turn without activating [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) again.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r7_Liu.JPG)  
*How much [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) damage would it take to stop a deck full of [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) and [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) s? Apparently the answer for Brian Liu, unfortunately, was just 16.* 

However, by this time Cox had (finally) found [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) . Combined with his seven lands in play, that was enough to search up [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) plus six [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) s. With Liu at 16 from casting [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) and a single attack from [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) , it was easily enough to take the first game.


Cox 1  Liu 0


### Game 2


With both players on seven to start the game again, the tables turned a bit. Liu started ramping early with a pair of [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) on his second and third turns, met only by a [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) from Cox.


[Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) took a short break from play thanks to [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) , but that merely freed Liu up to resolve [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) on his turn, immediately cashing in [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) for [Deceiver Exarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deceiver+Exarch) (untapping Pod) into [Glen Elendra Archmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glen+Elendra+Archmage) .


Ari Lax said earlier that this deck was the best deck in the format when [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) was in play, and Liu was clearly showing just how true that was, as Cox could merely look on and smirk.


The following turn Liu used [Glen Elendra Archmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Glen+Elendra+Archmage) to fetch up [Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zealous+Conscripts) (untapping [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) in the process), then used it again to grab [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) . When Liu demonstrated he knew how his combo worked (each new Conscripts untaps [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Kiki-Jiki%252C%2BMirror%2BBreaker) to make another Conscripts as much as you need), Cox scooped up his cards.




![Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker)![Zealous Conscripts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Zealous+Conscripts)

Basically, their combined text reads "You lose."



Cox 1  Liu 1


### Game 3


With both players at X-1, this was a very important game for both players. Lose, and they fall to the brink of missing the cut. Win, and they find themselves just one match away from guaranteeing a spot on Sunday.


But things didn't start well for Liu, pulling too many lands in his first hand and no Green mana in his all green spell-hand at 6. He kept his five, and with [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) in hand plus a number of creatures, he really couldn't ask for a better hand.


It got even better for him when Cox forgot the suspend trigger on a first turn [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) s, stranding it in limbo for an extra turn. Still, Cox barely missed a beat with a follow up [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) to keep the ramp going. If the match was going to come down to who could combo first, Cox still looked to be in good position.



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r7_cox.JPG)  
*Pat Cox going through the [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) motions: ramp, ramp, [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) , [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) , [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) . Game.* 

As expected, Liu played [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) on his turn, but was without the White mana necessary to cast [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) at instant speed to confound Cox's counters. Instead, he was forced to "settle" for a [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) , which Cox quickly [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) ed.


[Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek) found Cox an important seventh land the next turn while Liu still struggled to find White mana. With access to Red, Green and Blue mana (plus a very lonely [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) ), Liu's only real play was to try the Finks again. [Snap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snap) caster + [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) effectively shut the door on Liu's chances.


"Got me yet?" Liu asked.


"Looks like it," Cox said, floating mana to [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) eight lands away, finding plenty of [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle)s and [Mountain](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mountain) s to take the game and the match.


Cox 2  Liu 1


 
Saturday, 7:30 p.m. - Adapting to Jund
--------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
First at the Players' Championship; second at the Pro Tour; first, first and second at the last two Grands Prix.


Jund. Jund. Jund, Jund and Jund.


The most diabolical of midrange decks has certainly made its mark on Modern this year. Not necessarily dominating in number of Top 8 appearances, but definitely dominating in terms of taking the Trophy. And as more and more people pick up [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) , [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and the whole crew, it has become increasingly important to have a plan against the versatile, multi-pronged deck.


While some players \*cough\* [Channel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Channel) fireball \*ahem\* chose the "if you can't beat 'em, play Jund" strategy, a number of others made explicit decisions in their deck choices and individual card selections to fight back against the Red-Black-Green (and sometimes White) menace.


Take Pat Cox. Cox has been one of Jund's biggest proponents, playing it in every Modern event he's played in since Grand Prix Lincoln. But the surge in the deck's popularity left him looking elsewhere.


"I didn't want to play mirrors all day," Cox said. "I want to be on Jund, but the mirror is just random and 50/50."




![Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Bloodbraid+Elf)![Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Bloodbraid+Elf)

So, how do we settle this again?



Instead, Cox chose to play [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) , saying hate for the deck was at an all-time low, possibly making it a good choice for Toronto. He said he wasn't sure how he felt about the Jund match upironically having not played against it yetbut said he felt good about how he was doing so far.


Another player on [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) was Ben Stark, who said he didn't chose the deck because of any perceived strength against Jund [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) is something of a pet deck for Starkbut instead noted that almost no deck has a big advantage, or even a significant disadvantage, against Jund.


"Jund doesn't crush anything or get crushed by anything," Stark said.


"Except," he added, "by the various [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) decks."



![Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Birthing+Pod)

That's where some of our other heroes come in. Ari Lax and Alexander Hayne both chose [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) -based decks as ways to fight back against Jund, but for different reasons.


"I chose my deck because it beats Jund," Hayne said. "It's one of the few decks that actually crushes it."


Stark jumped in, agreeing with Hayne's assessment.


"It might be the only favorable matchup against Jund... because their creatures are all just value, value, value," Stark said.


Indeed, cards such as [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) , [Restoration Angel](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Restoration+Angel) , [Murderous Redcap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Murderous+Redcap) and more can be brutally effective against Jund's parade of mostly 1-for-1s. Because every [Terminate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminate) , [Abrupt Decay](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Abrupt+Decay) or [Maelstrom Pulse](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Maelstrom+Pulse) can actually put Jund behind a bit when Pod has already gotten value out of its creatures, it becomes fairly easy for either the [Melira, Sylvok Outcast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Melira%2C+Sylvok+Outcast) version or the [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) version to come out ahead on most trades against Jund.


But Lax played Pod for a completely different Jund-related reason. He had mostly been championing Poison decks as of late, but found that the addition of [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) to Jund slid that matchup from close to "How do I get past all those tokens?" bad. Instead, he chose to focus his deck choice on something that was both good against [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) and intrinsically powerful.


"With [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) in play, it's the best deck in the format," Lax said. "It's not even playing **Magic** anymore, you're just picking cards out of your deck and playing them."


But he also made a few subtle changes to help against Jund generally. One one-drop mana creature became a [Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wall+of+Roots) to possibly gum the ground while a second [Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kitchen+Finks) was added for even more resilience against removal. He even added two [Gavony Township](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gavony+Township) so that Jund couldn't ignore his smaller creatures while killing his larger ones.




![Kitchen Finks](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Kitchen+Finks)![Wall of Roots](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Wall+of+Roots)

Sometimes, all it takes is a few tweaks to swing a result in your favor.



Stark, though on board with the power of Pod decks, chose instead to play a deck that was pretty close pre-board, but far more favorable post-board.


Playing his pet [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) deck, Stark chose to focus on post-board games, where he sideboards in more than half his sideboard to completely change the landscape of the matchup. And since he feels the match is pretty close to begin withslightly favorable if they have just 2 [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) , slightly unfavorable if they have 4he seems to like those odds.


But, obviously, a number of players chose to stick with the consensus best deck because of the flexibility it gave them throughout the tournament, regardless of the matchup.


"I think, with any other deck, the matchups will determine how you do," Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa said, citing what happens if you play Affinity and your opponent draws two [Ancient Grudge](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ancient+Grudge) s early. "I didn't like that."


Instead, he chose Jund because it has game against pretty much everything.




![Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Dark+Confidant)![Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Tarmogoyf)

Yup, still good.



"It's powerful, it's good and doesn't have any cards that are so bad for it that it loses," he said, citing the lack of ways to hate out Jund.


Damo da Rosa is one the cusp of the cut at 5-2 after his three byes, but teammate Luis Scott-Vargas is 7-0 with the same exact deck.


So which result is more indicative of Jund's success this weekend? Stay tuned through the Top 8 on Sunday to find out just how prepared Toronto was to combat Jund's rise to the top.


 
Round 8 Feature Match - David Sharfman (Scapeshift) vs. Ben Stark (Scapeshift)
------------------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Mike Rosenberg*
David Sharfman and Ben Stark were fairly quiet as they sat down to play in their round 8 feature match. With both players at 18 points, a win would grand one of these two a lock in Day 2. The other player would have to win their next one to make it in, or finish just outside of contention in the final round.


To make matters more dire, both players would be going head-to-head in a [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) mirror match, making the need for more mana on the play much more important than in other match-ups. With their mind on the game, both players quickly got ready to see who could erupt [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle) the fastest!


### Game 1


After three rolls of the dice, Sharfman finally won the die roll and chose to play. Sharfman was quick to keep, while Stark took one good look at his hand and shuffled up for six instead. He kept his six card hand, and Sharfman led the action with a second-turn [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) . A second [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) stuck for Sharfman as Stark used [Peer Through Depths](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Peer+Through+Depths) to find [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) .


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r8_sharfman.jpg) *It's lots of lands and lots of shuffling in David Sharfman's match against Ben Stark.* 
Another land hit play for Stark, as Sharfman sacrficed a [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) to find an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) . He untapped and attacked Stark to 18, passing the turn and using [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) on upkeep targeting Stark's [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) . Stark was forced to [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) it, and [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) threatened to give Stark a chance at coming ahead on lands, with Sharfman temporarily stranded on land drops.


Sharfman sent his [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) away to get another [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) , but found no other lands to join it, suspending [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) and passing. When Start sacrificed his [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) , Sharfman used [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) to return Stark's [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle) to hand, setting him back a turn.


Sharfman found a land, putting a [Stomping Ground](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stomping+Ground) into play tapped as he passed back to Stark, who used [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) on Sharfman at the end of the turn. Stark added another land to play and passed back to Sharfman, who used an end-of-turn Cryptic Comand targeting Stark's [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Valakut%252C%2Bthe%2BMolten%2BPinnacle) once more. Stark responded with [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) , countering Sharfman's copy of the *Lorwyn* counterspell and drawing him a card.


Sharfman resolved his [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) , played a land, and cast [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) . When Stark's [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) was halted by [Izzet Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Charm) , Stark had enough and moved to the second game.


Sharfman 1  Stark 0


### Game 2


Stark led with [Stomping Ground](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stomping+Ground) , going to 18, as he suspended [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) . His ramp continued with [Farseek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Farseek) on the second turn, as two [Breeding Pool](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breeding+Pool) s hit play. Sharfman's first ramp spell came in the form of [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) . [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) from Stark bounced Sharfman's [Breeding Pool](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breeding+Pool) , but he was denied a land drop for the turn and passed with a shrug.


Sharfman ramped through the disruption with another [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) along with [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus) , while Stark found a land on the next turn to go with his [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) . The Elder became an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) at the end of Sharfman's turn, but no seventh land left Stark to pass. Sharfman played a land and passed, as Stark attempted [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) on one of Sharfman's lands at the end of the turn. Sharfman fought back with [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) . Stark countered back with [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) , but [Izzet Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Izzet+Charm) left Stark not resolving any spells. He played his bounced land, which returned to play after Sharfman's [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) , and passed back.


Sharfman attempted [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) , but it was [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) ed. [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) was Sharfman's only other play. Stark untapped, drew, played a tapped [Breeding Pool](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breeding+Pool) , and when he revealed [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) and [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) , Sharfman conceded to the lethal sorcery, with no way to fight through the [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) lying in wait.


Sharfman 1  Stark 1


### Game 3


Stark once again shipped his hand back on the draw, but this time, he stared at his six card hand with a wince. He showed off some lands, and then shipped it back for five.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r8_stark.jpg) *Stark quietly shuffles, hoping each time for a better hand, as he and Sharfman move into their third game.* 
Sharfman led with a suspended [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) , followed by a [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus) . Meanwhile, Stark had two lands that did not produce green mana. Sharfman's start showed little sign of slowing down as he got a land with his [Search for Tomorrow](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Search+for+Tomorrow) and cast [Sakura-Tribe Elder](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sakura-Tribe+Elder) . Stark, who kept playing lands, still lacked the necessary green mana to do much else.


Sharfman drew with his [Relic of Progenitus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Relic+of+Progenitus) , attacked Stark down to 18, and then passed after playing a land. [Cryptic Command](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cryptic+Command) from Sharfman at the end of Stark's turn bounced one of his opponent's lands and drew him a card. On the next turn, Scapeshfit with [Remand](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Remand) sealed the deal.


Sharfman 2  Stark 1


 
Round 98 Feature Match - William Jensen vs. Christian Sagermann
---------------------------------------------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
6-2. There's no more precarious place to be on Day 1 than sitting at two losses with just the last round to go. Win, and you're not only live for Day 2, but you still have a shot at the Top 8 and everything that comes with it.


Lose? You get to play in side events. To be fair, there are some pretty cool side events.


William "Huey" Jensen famously came within one vote of securing a spot in the **Magic** Hall of Fame last year, and a result this weekend would certainly do more to put him back on the minds of voters. Gamers who have played for a long time are quite familiar with Jensen, but younger players lack the familiarity with his resume that might have put him over the top. Succeeding this weekend with the Haunted Zoo deck he has been piloting would go a long way in that matter.


The man standing in front of him? Christian Sagermann.


The deck standing in his way? Jund. Of course.


Could it be any other way?


### Game 1


Sagermann led off by fetching an untapped [Overgrown Tomb](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Overgrown+Tomb) to play [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) , falling to 17 immediately, a difficult proposition against Jensen's heavily burn-based aggro deck.


Still, [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) is some good, and Jensen quickly cast [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) to take out Sagermann's one-drop.


Sagermann simply cast another one and passed back, before returning the favor the Jensen, [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) ing Jensen's attempt at a [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) of his own.


Still playing the same "Kill [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) " game, Jensen sent Sagermann's second one on a [Path to Exile](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Path+to+Exile) during the Jund player's upkeep. But Sagermann just kept right on going with a [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) ready to get started on offense and, if needed, defense.


Jensen, for his part, played his own [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) . Card for card, these two were at a stalemate at virtually every turn.


The Spirits traded the next turn as [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) discarded [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft) , and both players reloaded with the Flashback end of [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) .


Basically, it was a game of "anything you can do, I can do...well, pretty much the same."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r9_Jensen.jpg) *Trading spell-for-spell is not what William Jensen wanted to be doing against Jund.* 
That is, until Sagermann was able to play [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) in the same turn, threatening quite a bit of damage on his next attack.


At this point, life totals stood at 10-9 in favor of the Sagermann.


Sagermann didn't bite on the next attack, choosing not to activate [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) in the fact of untapped mana.


Jensen survived the turn by sending a [Lightning Helix](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Helix) straight at Sagermann. If he could get his Spirits through without trouble, [Tribal Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribal+Flames) would actually give him the win. If he drew it anyway...


Instead he draw [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) , which, in non-dramatic fashion, revealed [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) on the first card.


But Jensen was hardly out of it. He was still at 5 life and had plenty of blockers. He merely had to figure out if he could afford to attack and, if so, with what?


He eventually attacked with [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) , leaving back just two Spirits and [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) against a board of [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) , two Spirits and a [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) .


Though it served his purpose anyway, as Sagermann activated his [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) to block and trade with the Elf [Berserk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Berserk) er.


Blocks the next turn put Jensen at 4, but cost him both his Spirits. And when [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) cost Jensen his [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) , backed by a potential chump-blocking [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) , Jensen was effectively cold.


Sagermann 1  Jensen 0


### Game 2


Sagermann, now just one win away from Day 2, was forced to quickly throw back an unacceptable hand, but managed to settle on six as Jensen led with a [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) .


Thoughseize revealed Bloodbraid and...well, nothing. Four lands. Jensen had kept a five lander that suddenly became nothing but air, even as Jensen attacked for one with his Hierarch.


Sagermann's first move to clutter the battlefield was a [Fulminator Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fulminator+Mage) , something of a curious choice against Jensen's (usually) hyper aggressive deck. Still, it could potentially hit a key land for [Tribal Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribal+Flames) and, right now, it was certainly bigger than [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) .


But then Sagermann used it on Jensen's only red source in his upkeep...until [Blood Crypt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Blood+Crypt) gave Jensen another, plus the mana to cast [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft) .


A fourth land for Sagermann yielded, predictably, a [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) , springing forth a [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) from Sagermann's library.




|  |
| --- |
| 
Geist of Saint Traft
 |
| *[Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft) : Doing Work.*  |

Jensen had drawn a [Lightning Helix](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Helix) to help clear the way, but he was still pretty flooded. Nonetheless, the hit from the Geist and his Angel dropped Sagermann to just three life. [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) from Jensen made things even more precarious for the Jund mage.


Untapping and finding no help for the Hexproof Legend, Sagermann just shook his head and scooped up his cards, somehow losing a match he likely felt pretty good about post- [Thoughtseize](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Thoughtseize) .


Jensen 1 Sagermann 1


### Game 3


Back on the play for the deciding game, Sagermann's first play didn't come until he [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) ed Jensen's turn two [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) , which, in turn, gave Sagermann the breathing room to use [Fulminator Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Fulminator+Mage) to destroy Jensen's [Breeding Pool](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Breeding+Pool) .


Just how much that set Jensen back became apparent when Sagermann followed up with [Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Inquisition+of+Kozilek) .


[Inquisition of Kozilek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Inquisition%2Bof%2BKozilek) revealed [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) , two [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft) and a [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) , forcing the discard of the [Lightning Bolt](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Bolt) . Geist was obviously big game, but Sagermann cast a 4/5 [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) to start setting up a defense. Or, really, when your [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) is 4/5 on an empty board, a substantial offense.


Jensen dropped to 14 life to play a fetchland, predictably casting [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft) ...and nearly as predictably losing it to [Liliana of the Veil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Liliana+of+the+Veil) . Granted, this particular Liliana sprung forth from the top of Sagermann's deck, but it's a sequence of plays I've probably written 200 times if I've written it once.


The second Geist came down, but it didn't look like it would be enough. Sagermann sat forward in his chair, sensing this Day 2 berth was nearing. And when he cast both [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) and [Olivia Voldaren](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Olivia+Voldaren) before upping his Lilianaat no cost to himself I might addit looked like he was, in fact, on the verge.


Now down to five life, Jensen didn't have many options at his disposal. [Lightning Helix](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lightning+Helix) on Olivia would likely be the starting point of any comeback attempt, and that's exactly where he started. The subsequent attack put Sagermann to 11 life, and the flashback on [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls) gave Jensen at least a little room to work with.


Sagermann drew [Terminate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminate) off the top, giving him a multitude of options, but unsure how to sequence them, pausing and doing the math.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gptor12/r9_sagermann.jpg) *Christian Sagermann, even playing against one of the game's greats, found himself on the cusp of Day 2 in the last round of the day.* 
Eventually, Liliana forced Jensen to sacrifice a Spirit token and another one died to [Terminate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Terminate) , letting [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) put Jensen down to just three life. With [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) on his side of the board and still at 11 life, Sagermann had to like his position.


[Tribal Flames](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tribal+Flames) killed [Deathrite Shaman](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathrite+Shaman) , earning an activation to gain two life in response, but Jensen was forced to leave his Geist and newly cast [Noble Hierarch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Noble+Hierarch) back to chump block [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf) and [Raging Ravine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raging+Ravine) .


What could Jensen possibly have to stay in this, with no hand and no board at three life facing two threats?


The answer, apparently, was not


 
Top tables, a Day 1 overview
----------------------------


*by Blake Rasmussen*
Modern has proven to be an incredibly diverse format. Simply walking around the hall as the first rounds got underway, any observer could hardly mistake the sheer variety of archetypes available to any and all who wanted to sling some spells at Grand Prix Toronto.


Granted, some of those decks are less impressive than others. Merfolk, while occasionally a defensible choice, clearly hasn't been this weekend despite a number of adherents. And while Blue White Tron may have once been the bees knees, it has clearly been surpassed by its Red Green brethren.


To get a sense of how the top of the metagame ebbed and flowed throughout Day 1, we sampled the top 15 tables at various points to see what was doing well...and what fell off.


But first, here's a quite, Cliff's Notes version of what we're talking about when we label these decks ([you can find more detail here](http://www.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=mtg/daily/eventcoverage/gptor12/welcome#2)):


* Burnusually mono-Red, occasionally splash Black for [Bump in the Night](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bump+in+the+Night) and/or [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant) .
* Jundyou know. Jund. [Bloodbraid Elf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bloodbraid+Elf) , etc.
* Poisoncheap poison creatures and pump spells
* StormBlue and Red combo deck that kills with [Empty the Warrens](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Empty+the+Warrens) and/or [Grapeshot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grapeshot)
* RG TronRed and Green deck abusing [Urza's Tower](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Urza%27s+Tower) , Power Plant, and Mine
* UW Angela Blue-White Tempo/Control deck with flash creatures, countermagic and removal
* [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Splinter%2BTwin) [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Splinter+Twin) and [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) -based combo deck
* Robotsaggressive artifact deck with [Cranial Plating](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cranial+Plating)
* Haunted Zooa 5-color Zoo deck with [Lingering Souls](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lingering+Souls)
* Kiki Pod/Melira Poddecks abusing [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) , with one focusing on [Kiki-Jiki, Mirror Breaker](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kiki-Jiki%2C+Mirror+Breaker) combos and the other focusing on Melira, Sylvok Outcast combos
* EggsStanislav Cifka's Pro Tour *Return to Ravnica* winning combo deck
* Junkvarious flavors of Black Green White decks, often with [Doran, the Siege Tower](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Doran%2C+the+Siege+Tower) , but not always
* GW Little Kidvariations of Brian Kibler's hate bears deck. Usually marked by [Wilt-Leaf Liege](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wilt-Leaf+Liege)
* [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) a [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) -based [Valakut, the Molten Pinnacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Valakut%2C+the+Molten+Pinnacle) combo deck

Alright, with no more ado, on to the data!


### Round 3


Just one round before the pros get in, we see 13 distinct deck types. Jund is near the top, but so is Burn, as Burn is often a favorite of less experienced players for its ease of assembly and generally straight forward lines of play: namely, burn their face.


At a Grand Prix, this is the last round we would expect to see this kind of diversity if the format really revolved around just a handful of decks. The cream should quickly rise to the top.


However if the format is really this diverse? We could see some interesting things in subsequent rounds.


* Burn 7
* Jund 5
* Poison 2
* UR Storm 2
* RG Tron 2
* UW Angel 2
* Twin 2
* Haunted Zoo 2
* Kiki Pod 2
* Goblins 1
* Eggs 1
* Junk 1
* Robots 1

### Round 4


Notice anything? Yeah, Jund is a thing, and people with 3 byes seem to like it. Shamans is an aggressive Red Green deck, but it's not terribly important. It doesn't show up again.


And while Jund does far outpace the second best performing deck at this juncture, it's way too early with too small a sample size to make any judgments on it. But there are still a ton of deck archetypes out there.


* Jund 12
* Burn 3
* GW Little Kid 2
* Kiki Pod 2
* Robots 2
* UWR control 1
* Storm 1
* UR Delver 1
* Twin 1
* RG Tron 1
* Scapeshift 1
* Shamans 1

### Round 6


Two rounds later and Jund still seems to be performing. Several Red Green Tron decks started a hard charge in the middle rounds, but they would fall off along the way.


But notice the continued variety. Sure, Jund is obviously the by-the-numbers favorite, but there are still 11 archetypes near the top. The sixth round even featured a [Scapeshift](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scapeshift) mirror, of all things. Variety is the spice of life and, apparently, the rule in Modern.


* Jund 10
* RG Tron 5
* Scapeshift 3
* Burn 2
* Infect 2
* Infect 2
* Twin 2
* Haunted Zoo 1
* Kiki Pod 1
* Melira Pod 1
* Robots 1
* UR Control 1

### Round 8


After another two rounds, we see a bit more of a flattening of the Jund advantage. To a certain extent, this is to be expected as Jund mirrors knock each other off.


But, on the other hand, there are still a whopping 14 archetypes nearing the cut for Day 2. Jund has steadily dropped from nearly half of the top decks to under a fourth. That's still a large chunk, but decks like [Splinter Twin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Splinter%2BTwin) and the two flavors of [Birthing Pod](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Birthing+Pod) decks are certainly holding their own.


* Jund 7
* Twin 4
* Robots 2
* Kiki Pod 2
* Junk 2
* Burn 2
* RG Tron 2
* Haunted Zoo 2
* UW Angel 2
* WR control 1
* Poison 1
* Martyr 1
* Melira Pod 1
* Scapeshift 1

### Round 9


And in the final round of the day, the (completely unsurprising) winner is clearly Jund. Even as its numbers at the top tables slowly dipped over the course of the tournament, it managed to maintain its stranglehold over the numbers. We'll have a more complete metagame breakdown tomorrow for all of the Day 2 lists, but right now, Jund looks like the top-dog in terms of sheer numbers.


Still, the variety is still there. 12 distinct archetypes make up these top 30 lists, and a few others lurked just outside. Jund may be the safe, most reliable choice, but if Day 1 has shown us anything, it's certainly not the only choice.


* Jund 10
* Kiki Pod 2
* Melira Pod 2
* Scapeshift 3
* Haunted Zoo 3
* GW Hate Bears 2
* RG Tron 1
* Black White tokens 1
* BUG 1
* Eggs 1
* Storm 1
* Martyr 1
